                                      var result = '';

                <li><a href="#choices" title="Choices">Choices</a></li> 
                <li><a href="#choicesandgrammarbuilderappend" title="Choices and GrammarBuilder.Append">Choices and GrammarBuilder.Append</a></li> 
                <li><a href="#torecognizeallspeech">Dictation: to recognize ALL speech</a></li> 
               </ul> </li> 
              <li><a href="#promptbuilding" title="Prompt building">Prompt building</a></li> 
              <li><a href="#training">Training your speech recognition engine</a></li> 
              <li><a href="#history">History</a></li> 
             </ul> 
             <p><a name="disclaimer"></a></p>

If you don't have a English version of Windows, or non-English speech recognition, then you can use all code from this article, but then you need to change all words into the language of your speech recognizer.<br> <br> According to <a href="http://msdn.microsoft.com/en-us/library/system.speech.recognition.speechrecognitionengine%28v=vs.110%29.aspx" title="SpeechRecognition class MSDN">MSDN</a>[<a href="http://msdn.microsoft.com/en-us/library/system.speech.recognition.speechrecognitionengine%28v=vs.110%29.aspx" target="_blank" title="New Window">^</a>], the <code>SpeechRecognitionEngine</code> class is available in .NET 4.5, 4, 3.5, 3.0 and .NET 4 Client Profile, and the supported Windows versions are:</p>

             <p><a name="introduction"></a></p> 
             <h2><a name="introduction">Introduction</a></h2> 
             <p>In this article, I tell you how to program speech recognition, speech to text, text to speech and speech synthesis in C# using the <code>System.Speech</code> library.</p> 
             <p><a name="speechrecognitionincsharp"></a></p> 
             <h2><a name="speechrecognitionincsharp">Speech recognition in C#</a></h2> 
             <p><a name="speechrecognition">Speech recognition </a></p> 
             <p>To create a program with speech recognition in C#, you need to add the <strong>System.Speech</strong> library. Then, add this <code>using</code> namespace statement at the top of your code file:</p> 
             <pre lang="cs"><span class="code-keyword">using</span> System.Speech.Recognition;
<span class="code-keyword">using</span> System.Speech.Synthesis;
<span class="code-keyword">using</span> System.Threading;</pre> 
             <p>Then, create an instance of the <code>SpeechRecognitionEngine</code>:</p> 
             <pre lang="cs">SpeechRecognitionEngine _recognizer = <span class="code-keyword">new</span> SpeechRecognitionEngine();</pre> 
             <p>Then, we need to load grammars into the <code>SpeechRecognitionEngine</code>. If you don't do that, the speech recognizer will not recognize phrases. For example, add a grammar with the phrase "test" and we give the grammar the name "testGrammar":</p> 
             <pre lang="cs">_recognizer.LoadGrammar(<span class="code-keyword">new</span> Grammar(<span class="code-keyword">new</span> GrammarBuilder(<span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">test"</span>)) { Name = <span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">testGrammar"</span> }); <span class="code-comment">//</span><span class="code-comment"> load a grammar "test"</span></pre> 
             <p>Or:</p> 
             <pre lang="cs">Grammar gr = <span class="code-keyword">new</span> Grammar(<span class="code-keyword">new</span> GrammarBuilder(<span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">test"</span>));
gr.Name = <span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">testGrammar"</span>;
_recognizer.LoadGrammar(gr);</pre> 
             <p>If you don't want to give a name to the grammar, do this:</p> 
             <pre lang="cs">_recognizer.LoadGrammar(<span class="code-keyword">new</span> Grammar(<span class="code-keyword">new</span> GrammarBuilder(<span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">test"</span>))); <span class="code-comment">//</span><span class="code-comment"> load a "test" grammar</span></pre> 
             <p>Adding a name is only necessary if you want to unload a grammar in your program. To load grammars asynchronous, use the method <code>LoadGrammarAsync</code>. If you want to load a grammar while the recognizer is running, call the <a href="http://msdn.microsoft.com/en-us/library/system.speech.recognition.speechrecognitionengine.requestrecognizerupdate.aspx">RequestRecognizerUpdate method</a>[<a href="http://msdn.microsoft.com/en-us/library/system.speech.recognition.speechrecognitionengine.requestrecognizerupdate.aspx" target="_blank" title="New Window">^</a>] before loading the grammar, and load the grammar(s) in a <a href="https://msdn.microsoft.com/en-us/library/system.speech.recognition.speechrecognizer.recognizerupdatereached%28v=vs.110%29.aspx">RecognizerUpdateReached</a>[<a href="https://msdn.microsoft.com/en-us/library/system.speech.recognition.speechrecognizer.recognizerupdatereached%28v=vs.110%29.aspx" target="_blank">^</a>] event handler.</p> 
             <p>Then, add this event handler:</p> 
             <pre lang="cs">_recognizer.SpeechRecognized += _recognizer_SpeechRecognized;
</pre> 
             <p>If the speech is recognized, the method <code>_recognizer_SpeechRecognized</code> will be invoked. So, we need to create the method. What you can do, is when the program recognized the phrase "test", that you write "The test was successful!". To do that, use this:</p> 
             <pre lang="cs"><span class="code-keyword">void</span> _recognizer_SpeechRecognized(<span class="code-keyword">object</span> sender, SpeechRecognizedEventArgs e)
{
     <span class="code-keyword">if</span> (e.Result.Text == <span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">test"</span>) <span class="code-comment">//</span><span class="code-comment"> e.Result.Text contains the recognized text</span>
     {
         Console.WriteLine(<span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">The test was successful!"</span>);
     } 
} </pre> 
             <p>As you can see in the comment line, <code>e.Result.Text</code> contains the recognized text. That's useful if you've more then one grammar. But, the speech recognizer wasn't started. To do that, add this code after the <code>_recognizer.SpeechRecognized += _recognizer_SpeechRecognized </code>line:</p> 
             <pre lang="cs">_recognizer.SetInputToDefaultAudioDevice(); <span class="code-comment">//</span><span class="code-comment"> set the input of the speech recognizer to the default audio device</span>
_recognizer.RecognizeAsync(RecognizeMode.Multiple); <span class="code-comment">//</span><span class="code-comment"> recognize speech asynchronous</span></pre> 
             <p>Now, if we merge all methods, we get this:</p> 
             <pre lang="cs"><span class="code-keyword">static</span> <span class="code-keyword">void</span> Main(string[] args)
{
     SpeechRecognitionEngine _recognizer = <span class="code-keyword">new</span> SpeechRecognitionEngine();
     _recognizer.LoadGrammar(<span class="code-keyword">new</span> Grammar(<span class="code-keyword">new</span> GrammarBuilder(<span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">test"</span>)) Name = { <span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">testGrammar"</span> }); <span class="code-comment">//</span><span class="code-comment"> load a grammar</span>
     _recognizer.SpeechRecognized += _recognizer_SpeechRecognized; 
     _recognizer.SetInputToDefaultAudioDevice(); <span class="code-comment">//</span><span class="code-comment"> set the input of the speech recognizer to the default audio device</span>
     _recognizer.RecognizeAsync(RecognizeMode.Multiple); <span class="code-comment">//</span><span class="code-comment"> recognize speech asynchronous</span>
} 
<span class="code-keyword">void</span> _recognizer_SpeechRecognized(<span class="code-keyword">object</span> sender, SpeechRecognizedEventArgs e)
{
     <span class="code-keyword">if</span> (e.Result.Text == <span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">test"</span>) <span class="code-comment">//</span><span class="code-comment"> e.Result.Text contains the recognized text</span>
     {
         Console.WriteLine(<span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">The test was successful!"</span>);
     } 
} </pre> 
             <p>If you run that, it will not work. The program will be ended immediately. So, we must ensure that the program does not stop before the speech recognition is completed. We need to create a <code>ManualResetEvent</code> (<code>System.Threading.ManualResetEvent</code>), with the name <code>_completed</code>, and if the speech recognition is completed, we will call the <code>Set</code> method, and then the program will end. I loaded also a <code>"exit"</code> grammar. If the user says "exit", we will call the Set method. Because there're two threads, the Main thread and the speech recognition thread, we can pause the Main thread until the speech recognition thread isn't completed. And after the speech recognition is completed, we dispose the speech recognition engine (can take 3 seconds time at worst, at best 50 milliseconds):</p> 
             <pre lang="cs"><span class="code-keyword">static</span> ManualResetEvent _completed = <span class="code-keyword">null</span>;
<span class="code-keyword">static</span> <span class="code-keyword">void</span> Main(string[] args)
{
     _completed = <span class="code-keyword">new</span> ManualResetEvent(<span class="code-keyword">false</span>);
     SpeechRecognitionEngine _recognizer = <span class="code-keyword">new</span> SpeechRecognitionEngine();
     _recognizer.LoadGrammar(<span class="code-keyword">new</span> Grammar(<span class="code-keyword">new</span> GrammarBuilder(<span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">test"</span>)) Name = { <span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">testGrammar"</span> }); <span class="code-comment">//</span><span class="code-comment"> load a grammar</span>
     _recognizer.LoadGrammar(<span class="code-keyword">new</span> Grammar(<span class="code-keyword">new</span> GrammarBuilder(<span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">exit"</span>)) Name = { <span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">exitGrammar"</span> }); <span class="code-comment">//</span><span class="code-comment"> load a "exit" grammar</span>
     _recognizer.SpeechRecognized += _recognizer_SpeechRecognized; 
     _recognizer.SetInputToDefaultAudioDevice(); <span class="code-comment">//</span><span class="code-comment"> set the input of the speech recognizer to the default audio device</span>
     _recognizer.RecognizeAsync(RecognizeMode.Multiple); <span class="code-comment">//</span><span class="code-comment"> recognize speech asynchronous</span>
     _completed.WaitOne(); <span class="code-comment">//</span><span class="code-comment"> wait until speech recognition is completed</span>
     _recognizer.Dispose(); <span class="code-comment">//</span><span class="code-comment"> dispose the speech recognition engine</span>
} 
<span class="code-keyword">void</span> _recognizer_SpeechRecognized(<span class="code-keyword">object</span> sender, SpeechRecognizedEventArgs e)
{
     <span class="code-keyword">if</span> (e.Result.Text == <span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">test"</span>) <span class="code-comment">//</span><span class="code-comment"> e.Result.Text contains the recognized text</span>
     {
         Console.WriteLine(<span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">The test was successful!"</span>);
     } 
     <span class="code-keyword">else</span> <span class="code-keyword">if</span> (e.Result.Text == <span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">exit"</span>)
     {
         _completed.Set();
     }
}</pre> 
             <p>If you're programming a Windows application, you don't need to create a <code>ManualResetEvent</code>, because the UI thread ends only if the user closes the form.</p> 
             <p>To unload a grammar, use the method <code>UnloadGrammar </code>in the speech recognition engine, and to unload all grammars use the method <code>UnloadAllGrammars</code>. Don't forget to invoke the method <code>RequestRecognizerUpdate</code> and to load the grammars in a <code>RecognizerUpdateReached</code> event handler if the recognizer is running.<br> Unloading the "test" grammar for example:</p> 
             <pre lang="cs"><span class="code-keyword">foreach</span> (Grammar gr <span class="code-keyword">in</span> _recognizer.Grammars)
{
       <span class="code-keyword">if</span> (gr.Name == <span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">testGrammar"</span>)
       {
             _recognizer.UnloadGrammar(gr);
             <span class="code-keyword">break</span>;
       }
} </pre> 
             <ol> 
              <li>Create a grammar and load the grammar like this: <pre lang="cs">Grammar testGrammar = <span class="code-keyword">new</span> Grammar(<span class="code-keyword">new</span> GrammarBuilder(<span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">test"</span>));
_recognizer.LoadGrammar(testGrammar);  </pre> </li> 
              <li>Then, you can unload the grammar like this:</li> 
              <li>_recognizer.UnloadGrammar(testGrammar);</li> 
             </ol> 
             <p>If you unload a grammar with the second way, then you must ensure that all access modifiers are right. The first way is the easiest way, because if you use the first way, the access modifiers don't matter.</p> 
             <p><a name="speechrejected"></a></p> 
             <h3><a name="speechrejected">Speech rejected</a></h3> 
             <p>If you add a <code>SpeechRecognitionRejected</code> event handler to the <code>SpeechRecognitionEngine</code>, you can show candidate phrases found by the speech recognition engine. First, add a <code>SpeechRecognitionRejected</code> event handler:</p> 
             <pre>_recognizer.SpeechRecognitonRejected += _recognizer_SpeechRecognitionRejected;  </pre> 
             <p>Then, create the <code>_recognizer_SpeechRecognitionRejected</code> function:</p> 
             <pre lang="cs"><span class="code-keyword">static</span> <span class="code-keyword">void</span> _recognizer_SpeechRecognitionRejected(<span class="code-keyword">object</span> sender, SpeechRecognitionRejectedEventArgs e)
{
   <span class="code-keyword">if</span> (e.Result.Alternates.Count == <span class="code-digit">0</span>)
   {
     Console.WriteLine(<span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">Speech rejected. No candidate phrases found."</span>);
     <span class="code-keyword">return</span>;
   }
   Console.WriteLine(<span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">Speech rejected. Did you mean:"</span>);
   <span class="code-keyword">foreach</span> (RecognizedPhrase r <span class="code-keyword">in</span> e.Result.Alternates)
   {
    Console.WriteLine(<span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">    "</span> + r.Text);
   }
}</pre> 
             <p>This function shows all candidate phrases found by the speech recognition engine if the speech recognition was rejected.</p> 
             <p><a name="makesurethatthecomputerspeakstoyou"></a></p> 
             <h2><a name="makesurethatthecomputerspeakstoyou">Make sure that the computer speaks to you (text to speech)</a></h2> 
             <p>In the same library, there's a namespace <code>System.Speech.Synthesis</code>. In that namespace, you'll find a class <code>SpeechSythesizer</code>, and in the class there's a <code>Speak</code> method. Add the namespace add the top of your code file, and then try this:</p> 
             <pre lang="cs">SpeechSynthesizer _synthesizer = <span class="code-keyword">new</span> SpeechSynthesizer();
_synthesizer.Speak(<span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">Now the computer is speaking to you."</span>);</pre> 
             <p>If you run the code, the computer says: "Now the computer is talking to you." If you know that, you can use the speech recognition code, but instead of the test grammar use this grammar:</p> 
             <pre lang="cs">_recognizer.LoadGrammar(<span class="code-keyword">new</span> Grammar(<span class="code-keyword">new</span> GrammarBuilder(<span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">hello computer"</span>))); <span class="code-comment">//</span><span class="code-comment"> load a grammar</span></pre> 
             <p>And in the<code> _recognizer_SpeechRecognizer</code> method, add this:</p> 
             <pre lang="cs"><span class="code-keyword">void</span> _recognizer_SpeechRecognized(<span class="code-keyword">object</span> sender, SpeechRecognizedEventArgs e)
{
     <span class="code-keyword">if</span> (e.Result.Text == <span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">hello computer"</span>) <span class="code-comment">//</span><span class="code-comment"> e.Result.Text contains the recognized text</span>
     {
         SpeechSynthesizer synthesizer = <span class="code-keyword">new</span> SpeechSynthesizer();
         synthesizer.Speak(<span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">hello user"</span>);
         synthesizer.Dispose(); <span class="code-comment">//</span><span class="code-comment"> dispose the SpeechSynthesizer</span>
     }
     _completed.Set();
}  </pre> 
             <p>Use <code>SpeechSynthesizer.Dispose</code> to dispose the <code>SpeechSynthesizer</code>. Now, if you say "hello computer", the computer responds "hello user".</p> 
             <p><a name="emulatespeechrecognition"></a></p> 
             <h2><a name="emulatespeechrecognition">Emulate speech recognition</a></h2> 
             <p>It's also possible to emulate speech recognition with the <code>SpeechRecognitionEngine</code>. You can do that with the <code>EmulateRecognize</code> method, and to do it asynchronous, use the <code>EmulateRecognizeAsync</code> method:</p> 
             <pre lang="cs">RecognitionResult result = _recognizer.EmulateRecognize(<span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">test"</span>); <span class="code-comment">//</span><span class="code-comment"> not asynchronous, this does NOT invoke the _recognizer_SpeechRecognized method, because EmulateRecognize returns a RecognitionResult</span>

_recognizer.EmulateRecognizeAsync(<span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">test"</span>); <span class="code-comment">//</span><span class="code-comment"> asynchronous, invokes the _recognizer_SpeechRecognized method; the return type of EmulateRecognizeAsync is 'void'</span></pre> 
             <p>But a warning: You can't emulate speech recognition if the speech recognition engine is recognizing speech. So, you need to invoke this method before the method <code>RecognizeAsync</code> is invoked. You can also do it if the engine is ready with speech recognition.</p> 
             <p><a name="speechrecognizervsspeechrecognitionengine"></a></p> 
             <h2><a name="speechrecognizervsspeechrecognitionengine">SpeechRecognizer vs. SpeechRecognitionEngine</a></h2> 
             <p>In this article, I used the <code>SpeechRecognitionEngine</code> class. There's also a <code>SpeechRecognizer</code> class. So, what's the difference between the <code>SpeechRecognizer</code> class and the <code>SpeechRecognitionEngine</code> class? If you use the <code>SpeechRecognizer</code> class, you'll see the Windows Speech Recognizer:</p> 
             <p><img height="82" src="/KB/audio-video/483347/speechRecognizer.png" width="344"><br> If you use the <code>SpeechRecognitionEngine</code> class, you'll not see the Windows Speech Recognizer, the <code>SpeechRecognitionEngine</code> is the engine of a <code>SpeechRecognizer</code>. Also, the <code>SpeechRecognizer</code> class doesn't contain the methods <code>SetInputToDefaultAudioDevice</code> and <code>RecognizeAsync</code>.</p> 
             <p><a name="othertechniquesongrammarbuilding"></a></p> 
             <h2><a name="othertechniquesongrammarbuilding">Other techniques on grammar building</a></h2> 
             <p><a name="choices"></a></p> 
             <h3><a name="choices">Choices</a></h3> 
             <p>If you load more grammars, you can do this (here we load a phrase "dog", "cat" and "snake"):</p> 
             <pre lang="cs">_recognizer.LoadGrammar(<span class="code-keyword">new</span> Grammar(<span class="code-keyword">new</span> GrammarBuilder(<span class="code-keyword">new</span> Choices(<span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">dog"</span>,<span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">cat"</span>,<span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">snake"</span>))) { Name = <span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">animalGrammar"</span> });</pre> 
             <p>Advantages:</p> 
             <ul> 
              <li>The code is easier to read.</li> 
              <li>The <code>UnloadAllGrammars</code> function is faster.</li> 
             </ul> 
             <p>Disadvantages:</p> 
             <ul> 
              <li>If you unload a single grammar, you unload more then one phrase.</li> 
             </ul> 
             <p>You can also combine both ways to load grammars. For example you can load phrases like "dog", "cat", "snake" in a single grammar using <code>Choices</code>, because these are animals. But if you want to unload a single phrase, build only grammars with a single phrase. Instead of passing all phrases as parameters, we can use the <code>Add</code> method:</p> 
             <pre lang="cs">Choices animalChoices = <span class="code-keyword">new</span> Choices();
animalChoices.Add(<span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">dog"</span>);
animalChoices.Add(<span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">cat"</span>);
animalChoices.Add(<span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">snake"</span>);</pre> 
             <p>Or:</p> 
             <pre lang="cs">Choices animalChoices = <span class="code-keyword">new</span> Choices();
animalChoices.Add(<span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">dog"</span>, <span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">cat"</span>, <span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">snake"</span>); </pre> 
             <p><a name="choicesandgrammarbuilderappend"></a></p> 
             <h3><a name="choicesandgrammarbuilderappend">Choices and GrammarBuilder.Append </a></h3> 
             <p>It's possible that you want to load complete phrases like "I like dogs", "I dislike dogs", "I like cats", "I dislike cats", ... It's not a good idea to load all phrases separately. Using the <code>GrammarBuilder.Append</code> method, we can append <code>Choices</code> to the grammar builder:</p> 
             <pre>SpeechRecognitionEngine _recognizer = <span class="code-keyword">new</span> SpeechRecognitionEngine();<strong>
GrammarBuilder grammarBuilder = <span class="code-keyword">new</span> GrammarBuilder();
grammarBuilder.Append(<span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">I"</span>); <span class="code-comment">//</span><span class="code-comment"> add "I"</span>
grammarBuilder.Append(<span class="code-keyword">new</span> Choices(<span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">like"</span>, <span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">dislike"</span>)); <span class="code-comment">//</span><span class="code-comment"> load "like" &amp; "dislike"</span>
grammarBuilder.Append(<span class="code-keyword">new</span> Choices(<span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">dogs"</span>, <span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">cats"</span>, <span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">birds"</span>, <span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">snakes"</span>, 
   <span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">fishes"</span>, <span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">tigers"</span>, <span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">lions"</span>, <span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">snails"</span>, <span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">elephants"</span>)); <span class="code-comment">//</span><span class="code-comment"> add animals</span>
_recognizer.LoadGrammar(<span class="code-keyword">new</span> Grammar(grammarBuilder)); <span class="code-comment">//</span><span class="code-comment"> load grammar</span></strong>
_recognizer.SpeechRecognized += _recognizer_SpeechRecognized;
_recognizer.SetInputToDefaultAudioDevice(); <span class="code-comment">//</span><span class="code-comment"> set input to default audio device</span>
_recognizer.RecognizeAsync(RecognizeMode.Multiple); <span class="code-comment">//</span><span class="code-comment"> recognize speech</span></pre> 
             <p>If the user says "I like dogs",<code> _recognizer_SpeechRecognized</code> will be called. It will be called also if the user says "I like cats", "I like birds", "I dislike snails", ... Now, we can create the <code>_recognizer_SpeechRecognized</code> function. If the user says "I like cats", then "Do you really like cats?" is shown on the console, and if the user says "I dislike cats", then "Do you really dislike cats?" is shown on the console. <code>e.Result.Words[0].Text</code> is the first spoken word:</p> 
             <pre><span class="code-keyword">static</span> <span class="code-keyword">void</span> speechRecognitionWithChoices_SpeechRecognized(<span class="code-keyword">object</span> sender, SpeechRecognizedEventArgs e)
{
     Console.WriteLine(<span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">Do you really "</span> + e.Result.Words[1].Text + 
             <span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string"> "</span> + e.Result.Words[2].Text + <span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">?"</span>);
     manualResetEvent.Set();
}</pre> 
             <p><a name="torecognizeallspeech"></a></p> 
             <h3><a name="torecognizeallspeech">Dictation: to recognize ALL speech</a></h3> 
             <p>If you use a <code>DictationGrammar</code>, your program will recognize all speech using the Windows Desktop Speech technology. You can add a <code>DictationGrammar</code> and a "exit" grammar:</p> 
             <pre>SpeechRecognitionEngine _recognizer = <span class="code-keyword">new</span> SpeechRecognitionEngine();<strong>
_recognizer.LoadGrammar(<span class="code-keyword">new</span> Grammar(<span class="code-keyword">new</span> GrammarBuilder(<span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">exit"</span>)));</strong>
<strong>_recognizer.LoadGrammar(<span class="code-keyword">new</span> DictationGrammar());</strong>
_recognizer.SpeechRecognized += _recognizer_SpeechRecognized;
_recognizer.SetInputToDefaultAudioDevice(); <span class="code-comment">//</span><span class="code-comment"> set input to default audio device</span>
_recognizer.RecognizeAsync(RecognizeMode.Multiple); <span class="code-comment">//</span><span class="code-comment"> recognize speech </span></pre> 
             <p>And the <code>_recognizer_SpeechRecognized</code> method:</p> 
             <pre><span class="code-keyword">static</span> <span class="code-keyword">void</span> _recognizer_SpeechRecognized(<span class="code-keyword">object</span> sender, SpeechRecognizedEventArgs e)
{
    <span class="code-keyword">if</span> (e.Result.Text == <span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">exit"</span>)
    {
        manualResetEvent.Set();
        <span class="code-keyword">return</span>;
    }
    Console.WriteLine(<span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">You said: "</span> + e.Result.Text);
}</pre> 
             <p><code>new DictationGrammar()</code> returns an instance of the standard dictation grammar provided by Windows Desktop Speech technology.</p> 
             <h2><a id="promptbuilding">Prompt building</a></h2> 
             <p>Using a <code>System.Speech.Synthesis.PromptBuilder</code>, you can build prompt for the <code>SpeechSynthesizer</code>. You can add breaks, styles, sentences ... using the <code>PromptBuilder</code>.<br> Using the <code>StartSentence</code> and <code>EndSentence</code> method, you can indicate the start and the end of a sentence:</p> 
             <pre lang="cs">PromptBuilder builder = <span class="code-keyword">new</span> PromptBuilder();

builder.StartSentence();
builder.AppendText(<span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">This is a sentence."</span>);
builder.EndSentence();

SpeechSynthesizer synthesizer = <span class="code-keyword">new</span> SpeechSynthesizer();
synthesizer.Speak(builder);
synthesizer.Dispose();</pre> 
             <p lang="cs">Using the <code>AppendBreak</code> method, you can append a break:</p> 
             <pre lang="cs">PromptBuilder builder = <span class="code-keyword">new</span> PromptBuilder();

builder.StartSentence();
builder.AppendText(<span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">This is a sentence."</span>);
builder.EndSentence();

builder.AppendBreak(<span class="code-keyword">new</span> TimeSpan(<span class="code-digit">0</span>, <span class="code-digit">0</span>, <span class="code-digit">1</span>)); <span class="code-comment">//</span><span class="code-comment"> a break of 1 second</span>

builder.StartSentence();
builder.AppendText(<span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">This is another sentence."</span>);
builder.EndSentence();

SpeechSynthesizer synthesizer = <span class="code-keyword">new</span> SpeechSynthesizer();
synthesizer.Speak(builder);
synthesizer.Dispose();</pre> 
             <p lang="cs">Using the <code>StartStyle</code> and <code>EndStyle</code> method, you can indicate the style in the <code>PromptBuilder</code> (for example: loud, fast)</p> 
             <pre lang="cs">PromptBuilder builder = <span class="code-keyword">new</span> PromptBuilder();

builder.StartStyle(<span class="code-keyword">new</span> PromptStyle(PromptRate.Fast));
builder.AppendText(<span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">This text is spoken fast."</span>);
builder.EndStyle();

builder.StartStyle(<span class="code-keyword">new</span> PromptStyle(PromptVolume.ExtraSoft));
builder.AppendText(<span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">This text is spoken extra soft."</span>);
builder.EndStyle();

SpeechSynthesizer synthesizer = <span class="code-keyword">new</span> SpeechSynthesizer();
synthesizer.Speak(builder);
synthesizer.Dispose();</pre> 
             <p>Using the <code>StartVoice</code> and <code>EndVoice</code> method, you can indicate the voice, <em><strong>if installed</strong></em></p> 
             <pre>PromptBuilder builder = <span class="code-keyword">new</span> PromptBuilder();

builder.StartVoice(VoiceGender.Male, VoiceAge.Child);
builder.AppendText(<span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">This is a male child voice, if installed."</span>);
builder.EndVoice();

SpeechSynthesizer synthesizer = <span class="code-keyword">new</span> SpeechSynthesizer();
synthesizer.Speak(builder);
synthesizer.Dispose();</pre> 
             <p>On my computer, there's just one voice installed. So if I try another voice using the <code>StartVoice</code> method, then I don't get another voice.</p> 
             <p><a name="training"></a></p> 
             <h2><a name="training">Training your speech recognition engine</a></h2> 
             <p>This question is asked frequently in comments: how to train your speech recognition engine? From code, it is impossible, unfortunately. But you can train it through Windows Speech Recognition:</p> 
             <ol> 
              <li>Open <strong>Control Panel</strong></li> 
              <li>Go to <strong>Ease of Access</strong></li> 
              <li>Choose <strong>Speech Recognition</strong></li> 
              <li>Then choose <strong>Train your computer to better understand you</strong></li> 
             </ol> 
             <p>Then you'll see this form: <img alt="Image of speech recognition training" src="/KB/audio-video/483347/SpeechRecognitionVoiceTraining.png" style="margin: 5px"><br> Press <strong>Next</strong> and then the training begins. Speak the sentences aloud:<br> <img alt="Image of speech recognition training" src="/KB/audio-video/483347/SpeechRecognitionVoiceTraining2.png" style="margin: 5px"></p>

                              <td colspan="2">Hello<br> <br> I read your article but already in the beginning you do not explain well.<br> A lot of important information is missing in the introduction.<br> <br> 1.)<br> &gt; If the code isn't working for you, then some speech features aren't installed<br> <br> You don't write how to install these features.<br> Can I install chinese recognition on an english Windows at all?<br> <br> &gt; If you don't have a English version of Windows, or non-English speech recognition, <br> &gt; then you can use all code from this article, but then you need to change all <br> &gt; words into the language of your speech recognizer.<br> <br> What words are you talking about?<br> <code>"dog", "cat" and "snake" </code>?<br> So in a spanish operating system I have to translate these words into the spanish equivalents?<br> Why does Windows not already have a huge dictionary with all these words?<br> Why do I have to tell Windows these 3 words?<br> <br> 2.)<br> What does <code>new GrammarBuilder(new Choices("dog","cat","snake"))</code> do?<br> Do I tell the API to recognize nothing else than these 3 words?<br> And if I speak "car" it will not be understood by your code?<br> Does this API not allow to recognize ANY words?<br> I cannot see any sense in this line and sadly you don't explain it.<br> Your description is completely insufficient.<br> Instead of explaining well what this grammar is useful for you speak already about unloading the grammar. I did not even undertsand why you loaded these words at all.<br> <br> By the way: Three words are not even a grammar.<br> A grammar is a set of rules that explain how words are used in a language.<br> So "dog","cat","snake" surely is not a grammar.<br> <br> 3.)<br> Did you make any experiments with new Windows 10 API<br> <a href="https://msdn.microsoft.com/en-us/library/windows.media.speechrecognition.speechrecognizer.aspx">Windows.Media.SpeechRecognition.SpeechRecognizer</a>[<a href="https://msdn.microsoft.com/en-us/library/windows.media.speechrecognition.speechrecognizer.aspx" target="_blank" title="New Window">^</a>]<br> <br> I have the impression that this is the API that I'am looking for.<br> You speak some text and it gives you the recognition result in an event.<br> This API also allows to chose a language, as I expect a speech recognizer to do.<br> And I did not see that I have to load a grammar at all.<br></td>

                                <a rel="nofollow" onclick="return forumControl57022418.SwitchMessage(null,5294588);" href="/Messages/5294588/Sadly-a-not-well-explained-article.aspx"><img src="https://codeproject.global.ssl.fastly.net/App_Themes/CodeProject/Img/arrow-up24.png" title="Go to Parent" style="width:16px;height:16px;border:0"></a>
                               </div>Hello!<br> <br> 1) The article is about using the speech recognition services in C#. The installation of them in Windows is outside of the scope of this article - it's also something that I don't have experience with. You can do some research about this, I don't know this myself. The 'words' I'm talking about there, are, as you mentioned, for example "dog", "cat", and "snake". This makes sense because a Chinese speech recognizer won't understand "dog", "cat", and "snake".<br> 2) By your example, indeed you tell the API to recognize nothing else than these three words. Grammars are useful if you are only interested in those specific words. That makes sense, you shouldn't attempt to recognize words if you aren't interested in them. If you are interested in all words, use a DictationGrammar. I explain its usage later on in the article.<br> 3) I haven't done any experiments with this so far.<br>

                                </div>So what I understand is that this sort of speech recognition has been designed to recognize some specific words that I can give to the computer to instruct it do simple things like "Shut Down" or "Monitor Off" or something like that?
                               </blockquote><br> Not of you use a DictationGrammar. Please read that section of the article to learn more.<br> 
                               <blockquote class="quote">
                                <div class="op">
                                 Elmue wrote:
                                </div>You could give an example that is more usefull in the real life than recognizing three animals.
                               </blockquote><br> The current animal example is perfect for the article, in my opinion. It's easy to adjust in case you want to do something with spoken commands, such as "Shut Down" or "Monitor Off", and it's simple enough that the focus stays on the speech recognition part, not on hwat happens if you recognize something.<br>

                              <td colspan="2">If you use RequestRecognizerUpdate, I think you should then use RecognizerUpdateReached event handler to call LoadGrammar, plus you would do all LoadGrammar calls together in that event handler. <br> <br> Of course if the recognizer is not started yet, there shouldn't be any need to call RequestRecognizerUpdate in the first place (can remove it)<br>

                               </div>It would be possible, but you'd have to rewrite the current function: as it currently stands, the associated objects are made for one-time use, not for re-use. You could do something like this: put the switch statement in a separate function (and call that function from everywhere you need it), and at the beginning of this method, make sure that if the objects (recognizer, synthesizer, ...) are still active, that they are disabled and re-created, and then let the user choose.<br>

$(document).ready(function() {
 if(InitWatermark)InitWatermark('sb_tb', 'Search for articles, questions, tips');
 var sbar = $('#sb_tb'); 
 var sfilter = $('#SearchFilter');
 if (sbar && sfilter) {
  sfilter.removeClass('popup'); sfilter.hide(); sfilter.removeClass('open');
  sbar.blur(function() {
 if (!oSrchFlt) {sfilter.hide(); sfilter.removeClass('open');}
 srchBoxFoc=false;
 });
  sbar.focus(function() {
 oSrchFlt=false; srchBoxFoc=true;
 sfilter.show(); sfilter.addClass('open');
 });
  sbar.mouseleave(function() { oSrchBox=false; });
  sbar.mouseover(function() { oSrchBox=true; });
  sfilter.mouseleave(function() { oSrchFlt=false; if (!srchBoxFoc&&!oSrchBox) { sfilter.hide(); sfilter.removeClass('open'); }});
  sfilter.mouseover(function() { oSrchFlt=true; });
 }
});

                        function getVotesHistogram(objectId, objectTypeId, containerId, loadingId) {
                            if (!$('#' + containerId).attr('alreadyRequested')){
                                $.ajax({
                                    url: '/script/Ratings/Ajax/Histogram.aspx?obid=' + objectId + '&obtid='+objectTypeId,
                                    success: function (data) {
                                        $('#' + containerId).html(data);
                                        $('#' + loadingId).hide();
                                    }
                                });
                                $('#' + containerId).attr('alreadyRequested', 'true');
                            }
                        }
